@@ -0,0 +1,271 @@
+# SK8Lytz Payload Reference
+> Last updated: April 8, 2026  
+> All payloads we BUILD OURSELVES (pixel-by-pixel, byte-by-byte) ΓÇö not pass-through hardware modes
+
+---
+
+## ≡ƒöº Packet Wrapper (Applied to Every Command)
+
+Before any command hits the wire, `ZenggeProtocol.wrapCommand()` prepends an 8-byte BLE header:
+
+```
+[0x00] [SEQ] [0x80] [0x00] [LEN_HI] [LEN_LO] [LEN+1] [0x0B] [...payload]
+```
+
+| Byte | Value | Meaning |
+|------|-------|---------|
+| `00` | `0x00` | Packet start |
+| `01` | `SEQ` | Rolling counter 0ΓÇô255, increments each send |
+| `02` | `0x80` | Fixed protocol flag |
+| `03` | `0x00` | Reserved |
+| `04ΓÇô05` | `LEN_HI/LO` | 16-bit payload length |
+| `06` | `LEN+1` | Length overflow byte |
+| `07` | `0x0B` | Command family ID |
+| `08+` | Payload | The actual command payload |
+
+> [!NOTE]
+> Checksum is always the last byte of the payload, calculated as: `sum(all_payload_bytes) & 0xFF`
+
+---
+
+## ≡ƒôª PAYLOAD 1: `0x59` ΓÇö MultiColor Pixel Array (Our Primary Tool)
+
+**Used by**: Multimode Patterns 1ΓÇô5 & 9ΓÇô10, Street Mode, Emergency Mode, Solid Color, DIY Array  
+**Source**: `ZenggeProtocol.setMultiColor()`
+
+### Byte Layout
+
+```
+[0x59] [LEN_HI] [LEN_LO]
+  [R0] [G0] [B0]              ΓåÉ LED 0  (pixel 0 color)
+  [R1] [G1] [B1]              ΓåÉ LED 1
+  ...                          ΓåÉ ... (one R/G/B triple per LED)
+  [Rn] [Gn] [Bn]              ΓåÉ LED n  (full LED count)
+[PTS_HI] [PTS_LO]             ΓåÉ numPoints (total LED count, 16-bit BE)
+[TRANS]                        ΓåÉ transitionType (see table below)
+[SPEED]                        ΓåÉ animation speed 1ΓÇô31
+[DIR]                          ΓåÉ direction: 1=forward, 0=reverse
+[CHECKSUM]
+```
+
+### Total Length
+`totalLen = (numLEDs ├ù 3) + 9`  
+e.g. HALOZ 16 LEDs ΓåÆ 57 bytes. SOULZ 43 LEDs ΓåÆ 138 bytes.
+
+### Transition Type Byte (Hardware-Confirmed)
+
+| Value | Constant | Behavior |
+|-------|----------|----------|
+| `0x00` | CASCADE | Freezes pattern statically ΓÇö do NOT use for animations |
+| `0x01` | FREEZE | Locks array in place ΓÇö static output, no scrolling |
+| `0x02` | STROBE | Hardware strobes entire array on/off |
+| `0x03` | RunningWater | Hardware scrolls/cascades the pixel array Γ£à animations |
+
+### Speed Range
+- Animated types (`0x03`): clamped `1ΓÇô31` (from APK Protocol/n.java)
+- Static/Freeze (`0x01`): always sends `1` (speed unused)
+
+### Color Rule
+> [!IMPORTANT]
+> **SEND PURE RGB** ΓÇö do NOT call `applyColorSorting()` before building 0x59 payload.  
+> The hardware remaps GRB internally via its 0x81/0x62 config register.  
+> Exception: DIY Array mode intentionally applies sorting because those colors are user-chosen hex strings.
+
+---
+
+## ≡ƒôª PAYLOAD 2: `0x51` ΓÇö DIY Custom Mode (2-Step Hardware Fade/Flash)
+
+**Used by**: Multimode Patterns 6 (Breath), 7 (Flash), 8 (Strobe)  
+**Source**: `ZenggeProtocol.setCustomMode()`
+
+### Byte Layout
+
+```
+[0x51]
+  [STEP_FLAG] [MODE] [SPEED] [FG.R] [FG.G] [FG.B] [BG.R] [BG.G] [BG.B]   ΓåÉ Step 0 (9 bytes)
+  [STEP_FLAG] [MODE] [SPEED] [FG.R] [FG.G] [FG.B] [BG.R] [BG.G] [BG.B]   ΓåÉ Step 1 (9 bytes)
+  ... ├ù 32 steps total (inactive steps = 0x0F + 8 zeros)
+[0x0F]        ΓåÉ Terminator
+[CHECKSUM]
+```
+
+**Total size: always 291 bytes** (32 steps ├ù 9 bytes + 0x51 header + 0x0F + checksum)
+
+### Step Mode Values
+
+| Value | Constant | Effect |
+|-------|----------|--------|
+| `0x3A` | STEP_JUMP | Hard cut (instant color change) |
+| `0x3B` | STEP_GRADUAL | Smooth fade/crossfade |
+| `0x3C` | STEP_STROBE | Rapid flash |
+
+> [!WARNING]
+> Using `0x01` or `0x02` as step mode sends wrong bytes. Must use `0x3A`, `0x3B`, `0x3C`.
+
+### How Patterns 6, 7, 8 use 0x51
+
+| Pattern | Steps | Mode | Behavior |
+|---------|-------|------|----------|
+| **6 Breath** | Step0: FGΓåÆBG, Step1: BGΓåÆFG | `STEP_GRADUAL (0x3B)` | Hardware loops smooth fade |
+| **7 Flash** | Step0: FGΓåÆBG, Step1: BGΓåÆFG | `STEP_JUMP (0x3A)` | Hardware loops hard cuts |
+| **8 Strobe** | Step0: FGΓåÆBG, Step1: BGΓåÆFG | `STEP_JUMP (0x3A)` at speed=100 | Max rate hard flash |
+
+---
+
+## ≡ƒÄ¿ PAYLOAD 3: Solid Color (`sendColor`)
+
+**Used by**: Any mode that sends a single flat color (color picker, brightness slider, etc.)  
+**Source**: `DockedController.sendColor(r, g, b)`
+
+**How it's built:**
+```
+colors = Array(numLEDs).fill({ r, g, b })
+ZenggeProtocol.setMultiColor(colors, speed=1, direction=1, transitionType=0x01)
+```
+
+- Same structure as PAYLOAD 1 (0x59)
+- All pixels identical color
+- `transitionType=0x01` (FREEZE) ΓÇö no animation, immediate static output
+- Speed always `1` (unused for freeze)
+
+---
+
+## ≡ƒö▓ PAYLOAD 4: Multimode Patterns (PatternEngine pixel tiles)
+
+**Used by**: Fixed Mode / Multimode ΓåÆ Patterns 1ΓÇô5, 9ΓÇô10  
+**Source**: `DockedController.applyFixedPattern()` ΓåÆ `PatternEngine.buildPatternPayload()`
+
+### How patternId maps to a pixel tile (tiled to full strip length)
+
+| Pattern | Name | Pixel Tile (FG=foreground, BG=background) | Protocol | TransitionType |
+|---------|------|-------------------------------------------|----------|----------------|
+| **1** | Solid | `[FG]` ΓÇö tiled | `0x59` | `0x01` FREEZE |
+| **2** | Single Dot | `[FG, BG, BG, BG, BG, BG, BG, BG]` ΓÇö 1 dot in 7 bg | `0x59` | `0x03` RunningWater |
+| **3** | Comet | `[FG, FG├ù0.5, FG├ù0.2, BG, BG, BG]` ΓÇö FG + 2-step dim trail | `0x59` | `0x03` RunningWater |
+| **4** | Dashed | `[FG, FG, FG, FG, BG, BG, BG, BG]` ΓÇö 4-on 4-off | `0x59` | `0x03` RunningWater |
+| **5** | Alternating | `[FG, FG, BG, BG]` ΓÇö 2-on 2-off | `0x59` | `0x03` RunningWater |
+| **6** | Breath | *(no pixel array)* | `0x51` GRADUAL | N/A |
+| **7** | Flash | *(no pixel array)* | `0x51` JUMP | N/A |
+| **8** | Strobe | *(no pixel array)* | `0x51` JUMP max speed | N/A |
+| **9** | Wave | `[BG, BG, FG, FG, BG, BG]` ΓÇö FG pair in BG field | `0x59` | `0x03` RunningWater |
+| **10** | Pinch | `[FG, BG, BG, BG, BG, FG]` ΓÇö FG at each end | `0x59` | `0x03` RunningWater |
+
+### Brightness: applied before tile construction
+```
+fgRgb.r = Math.round(parseInt(fgHex.r) * (brightness / 100))
+```
+
+### Speed: UI 0ΓÇô100 ΓåÆ Hardware 1ΓÇô31
+```
+hwSpeed = Math.round((uiSpeed / 100) * 31)  // clamped min=1, max=31
+```
+
+---
+
+## ≡ƒÄ┐ PAYLOAD 5: Street Mode ΓÇö Car Light Layout
+
+**Used by**: Street Mode (accelerometer-reactive)  
+**Source**: `DockedController.applyStreetPattern()`  
+**Protocol**: `0x59` via `ZenggeProtocol.setMultiColor(arr, hwSpeed, 1, transType)`
+
+### Zone Layout
+
+**HALOZ** (2-segment ring, 16 LEDs ΓÇö 8-LED mirrored frame):
+```
+Frame8:  [RED, RED, CRUISE, CRUISE_DIM, CRUISE, CRUISE_DIM, WHITE, WHITE]
+Mirror8: [WHITE, WHITE, CRUISE_DIM, CRUISE, CRUISE_DIM, CRUISE, RED, RED]
+Result:  RED at back of ring, WHITE at front, CRUISE color on both sides
+```
+
+**SOULZ** (linear strip, N LEDs ΓÇö zone proportions):
+```
+[rear 30% = RED tail lights]
+[mid 40%  = alternating CRUISE / CRUISE_DIM (zebra)]
+[front 30% = WHITE headlights]
+```
+
+### Motion State ΓåÆ Color Mapping
+
+| Motion State | Cruise Color | Tail Brightness | TransitionType |
+|-------------|-------------|-----------------|----------------|
+| CRUISING | User's chosen color (default `#FF8C00` amber) | 45% dim red | `0x01` FREEZE |
+| ACCELERATING | User's chosen color | 45% dim red | `0x01` FREEZE |
+| SLOWING_DOWN | `#FFFF00` Yellow | 45% dim red | `0x01` FREEZE |
+| STOPPED | `#FF0000` Red | Full red | `0x01` FREEZE |
+| HARD_BRAKING | `#FF0000` Red | Full red | `0x02` STROBE |
+
+> [!NOTE]
+> `0x01` (FREEZE) is used for CRUISE/STOP so the headlight/taillight zones stay physically locked in position.
+> `0x02` (STROBE) is only used for HARD_BRAKING to flash the entire array as an emergency signal.
+
+---
+
+## ≡ƒÜ¿ PAYLOAD 6: Emergency Alert Pattern
+
+**Used by**: Programs mode Pattern ID 100, and Emergency Alert button  
+**Source**: `DockedController.applyEmergencyPattern()`  
+**Protocol**: `0x59` with `transitionType=0x03` (RunningWater ΓÇö hardware scrolls)
+
+**HALOZ** (16-LED ring):
+```
+Frame8:  [RED, RED, YELLOW, OFF, YELLOW, OFF, WHITE, WHITE]
+Mirror:  [WHITE, WHITE, OFF, YELLOW, OFF, YELLOW, RED, RED]
+```
+
+**SOULZ** (linear):
+```
+[RED, RED, RED, RED, YELLOW, OFF, YELLOW, OFF, YELLOW, OFF, YELLOW, OFF, WHITE, WHITE, WHITE, WHITE]
+```
+
+Hardware scrolls this with `0x03` (RunningWater) ΓÇö so the red/yellow/white zones cycle visually around the strip.
+
+---
+
+## ≡ƒîê PAYLOAD 7: DIY Array (User-Built Color Sequence)
+
+**Used by**: Multimode ΓåÆ DIY Array sub-mode  
+**Source**: `DockedController` speed slider `onSlidingComplete` + DIY Array Builder component
+
+```js
+rgbColors = multiColors.map(hexColor => {
+  // Parse hex ΓåÆ RGB, scale by brightness factor
+  rawR = parseInt(hex.r) * brightnessFactor
+  // Then COLOR SORT (unlike other modes, DIY applies sorting):
+  return ZenggeProtocol.applyColorSorting(rawR, rawG, rawB, hwSettings.colorSorting)
+})
+ZenggeProtocol.setMultiColor(rgbColors, clampSpeed(speed), direction=1, multiTransition)
+```
+
+> [!IMPORTANT]
+> **DIY Array DOES apply `applyColorSorting()`** ΓÇö this is intentional and correct here because the user is picking colors manually by name ("red", "green") and the hardware needs the channels swapped to display them right. All other modes skip this.
+
+### `multiTransition` options in DIY mode
+
+| Value | Visual Effect |
+|-------|--------------|
+| `0x01` | FREEZE ΓÇö static array (no scroll) |
+| `0x03` | RunningWater ΓÇö hardware scrolls colors around the strip |
+
+---
+
+## ≡ƒôí Other Utility Commands (Not Custom-Built Payloads)
+
+| Command | Payload | Purpose |
+|---------|---------|---------|
+| **Power On** | `[0x71, 0x23, 0x0F, 0xA3]` | Turns all LEDs on |
+| **Power Off** | `[0x71, 0x24, 0x0F, 0xA4]` | Turns all LEDs off |
+| **Query HW Settings** | `[0x63, 0x12, 0x21, 0x0F, CS]` | Request device's IC, LED count, color order |
+| **Programs/RBM** | `0x61` via `setCustomRbm(patternId, speed, brightness)` | Select one of 210 built-in hardware patterns by ID |
+| **Music Mode** | `0x73` via `setMusicConfig(...)` | Configure mic-reactive symphony mode |
+
+---
+
+## ≡ƒöæ Key Rules Summary
+
+1. **Always send PURE RGB** in `0x59` (except DIY Array which uses sorted colors)
+2. **Animated patterns need `0x03`** ΓÇö `0x00` appears to be CASCADE but actually FREEZES the array
+3. **Static/solid needs `0x01`** ΓÇö locks the exact pixel positions sent  
+4. **STROBE `0x02`** flashes the whole array ΓÇö only for hard braking emergency  
+5. **Speed for 0x59**: UI `0ΓÇô100` ΓåÆ hardware `1ΓÇô31` via `clampSpeed()`
+6. **Speed for 0x51** (DIY step mode): full `1ΓÇô100` range valid
+7. **LED count = `hwSettings.ledPoints`** ΓÇö do NOT divide by segments (segments is an IC layout param, not a pixel-count divisor)

+
+## COLOR SORTING ΓÇö ARCHITECTURE & RULES
+
+> [!CAUTION]
+> The hardware does NOT auto-remap pixel bytes based on 0x62 colorSorting config.
+> The app MUST pre-swap RGB bytes in software before sending any 0x59 payload.
+> Failure to do this causes RΓåöG channel inversion on GRB-wired strips (HALOZ / SOULZ).
+
+### How colorSorting flows
+```
+[Device 0x63 response] ΓåÆ parseHardwareSettingsResponse() ΓåÆ colorSorting (numeric)
+      Γåô
+[DashboardScreen] setAllDevices() / setDeviceConfigs() stores colorSorting per device ID
+      Γåô
+[activeHwSettings useMemo] (DashboardScreen L1132) builds hwSettings prop:
+  - detected=true  ΓåÆ use d.colorSorting from probed hardware response
+  - detected=false ΓåÆ use sortingIdx derived from device name string ('GRB' ΓåÆ 2)
+      Γåô
+[DockedController] receives hwSettings.colorSorting (numeric)
+      Γåô
+All payload builders call: ZenggeProtocol.applyColorSorting(r, g, b, hwSettings.colorSorting ?? 2)
+```
+
+### applyColorSorting Index Map (ZenggeProtocol.ts)
+| Index | Name | Byte order sent to hardware |
+|:---|:---|:---|
+| 0 | RGB | R, G, B |
+| 1 | RBG | R, B, G |
+| 2 | **GRB** ΓåÉ HALOZ/SOULZ default | G, R, B |
+| 3 | GBR | G, B, R |
+| 4 | BRG | B, R, G |
+| 5 | BGR | B, G, R |
+
+> [!NOTE]
+> HALOZ and SOULZ are both WS2812B strips wired in GRB order ΓåÆ `colorSorting = 2`.
+> If the device hasn't been probed (detected=false), always assume GRB (2) as fallback.
+
+### Functions that MUST call applyColorSorting before setMultiColor
+| Function | File | Status |
+|:---|:---|:---|
+| `applyFixedPattern()` | `DockedController.tsx` | Γ£à applied to fgRgb/bgRgb |
+| `sendColor()` | `DockedController.tsx` | Γ£à fixed Apr 2026 |
+| `applyStreetPattern()` | `DockedController.tsx` | Γ£à fixed Apr 2026 |
+| `generateSortedColors()` | `DockedController.tsx` | Γ£à applied |
+| DIY multicolor slice handlers | `DockedController.tsx` L2232/2282 | Γ£à applied |
+| `loadFavorite()` DIY path | `DockedController.tsx` L770 | Γ£à applied |
+| `setColor()` in ZenggeProtocol | `ZenggeProtocol.ts` L366 | ΓÜá∩╕Å does NOT sort ΓÇö only use for testing |
+
+---
+
+## 0x59 TRANSITION TYPES ΓÇö COMPLETE REFERENCE
+
+> [!IMPORTANT]
+> There are TWO completely separate transition type systems. Never mix them.
+
+### 0x59 setMultiColor ΓÇö `transitionType` parameter
+| Byte | Name | Description | Use case |
+|:---|:---|:---|:---|
+| `0x00` | **Static** | Freeze array in place, no animation | Solid colors, car lights, any non-moving pattern |
+| `0x01` | **Gradual** | Smooth crossfade between pixel states | Breathing-style animations on pixel arrays |
+| `0x02` | **Strobe** | Flash entire array on/off rapidly | Emergency braking, alert states |
+| `0x03` | **RunningWater** | Hardware scrolls pixel array around strip | Chasing/marquee patterns (dots, comets, dashes) |
+
+### 0x51 setCustomMode ΓÇö step `mode` field
+| Byte | Constant | Description | Use case |
+|:---|:---|:---|:---|
+| `0x3A` | `STEP_JUMP` | Hard-cut between step colors | Flash (Pattern 7), Strobe (Pattern 8) |
+| `0x3B` | `STEP_GRADUAL` | Smooth fade between step colors | Breath (Pattern 6) |
+| `0x3C` | `STEP_STROBE` | Rapid flash between step colors | Not currently used |
+
+> [!WARNING]
+> `0x3A/3B/3C` are ONLY valid in `setCustomMode()` (0x51 command).
+> `0x00/01/02/03` are ONLY valid in `setMultiColor()` (0x59 command).
+> Passing 0x3A/3B/3C to setMultiColor sends garbage transitionType bytes to hardware.
+
+### Street Mode Transition Types (fixed Apr 2026)
+| Motion State | transitionType | Rationale |
+|:---|:---|:---|
+| STOPPED | `0x00` Static | Brake lights on, no movement |
+| CRUISING | `0x00` Static | Car light arrangement stays fixed |
+| SLOWING_DOWN | `0x00` Static | Yellow warning lights, no movement |
+| ACCELERATING | `0x00` Static | Normal riding lights, no movement |
+| HARD_BRAKING | `0x02` Strobe | Urgent flashing for safety |
+
+### Pattern Engine Transition Types (PatternEngine.ts)
+| Pattern | transitionType | Rationale |
+|:---|:---|:---|
+| 1 ΓÇö Solid | `0x00` Static | No movement by definition |
+| 2ΓÇô5, 9ΓÇô10 | `0x03` RunningWater | Hardware scrolls the tiled pattern |
+| 6 ΓÇö Breath | 0x51 `STEP_GRADUAL` | Two-step fade FGΓåöBG |
+| 7 ΓÇö Flash | 0x51 `STEP_JUMP` | Two-step hard-cut FGΓåöBG |
+| 8 ΓÇö Strobe | 0x51 `STEP_JUMP` @speed=100 | Two-step max-speed flash |

+∩╗┐# SK8Lytz App: System Master Reference (EXHAUSTIVE)
+
+This is the definitive technical manual for the SK8Lytz LED control system. It consolidates all protocol specifications, pattern listings, hardware configurations, and implementation details necessary for development. **DO NOT SHORTEN THIS DOCUMENT.**
+
+---
+
+## 1. System Overview & Architecture
+The SK8Lytz ecosystem provides high-performance, professional-grade LED control for roller skates.
+- **Platform**: React Native (Expo)
+- **Communication**: Bluetooth Low Energy (BLE) via `react-native-ble-plx`
+- **Protocol**: Zengge / Magic Home / LEDnetWF (V2 Packet Wrapper)
+- **Visualizer**: High-fidelity React Native `Canvas` / `View` based LED simulation.
+
+---
+
+## 2. Hardware Specifications
+
+
+
+### Product Scope ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ App Compatibility
+| Product | App Compatible | Reason |
+|:---|:---|:---|
+| **SOULZ** | YES | Zengge BLE controller, WS2812B, full protocol support |
+| **HALOZ** | YES | Zengge BLE controller, WS2812B, full protocol support |
+| **CLIPZ** | NO | Not smart / not Bluetooth. RF remote only. Cannot connect to app. No app development needed. |
+### Device Profiles
+
+| Profile | LED Count | IC Type | Default Color Order | Usage |
+|:---|:---|:---|:---|:---|
+| **HALOZ** | 16 | WS2812B | GRB (`0x03`) | Wheel / Frame Ring |
+| **SOULZ** | 43 | WS2812B | GRB (`0x03`) | Boot / Sole Strip |
+
+### Hardware Configuration Command (`0x81`)
+Executed upon connection to ensure software-to-hardware pixel alignment.
+- **Hex Header**: `0x81`
+- **Payload Structure**: `[0x81, PointsHigh, PointsLow, ColorOrder, IcType, 0x00, 0x00, Checksum]`
+- **Color Order Key**: `RGB=1, RBG=2, GRB=3, GBR=4, BRG=5, BGR=6`
+- **Example (HALOZ GRB)**: `[0x81, 0x00, 0x10, 0x03, 0x03, 0x00, 0x00, 0x97]`
+
+---
+
+## 3. Protocol Deep-Dive (Zengge V2)
+
+### A. The V2 Packet Wrapper
+All raw commands must be wrapped in this 8-byte header before transmission.
+
+| Byte | Field | Description |
+|:---|:---|:---|
+| 0 | Version | `0x00` (Version 0) |
+| 1 | Sequence | Incremental ID (`messageCounter++ % 256`) |
+| 2-3 | Flags | `0x80 0x00` (No segmentation) |
+| 4-5 | Total Length | Raw Payload Length (Big Endian) |
+| 6 | Cmd Length | `RawPayloadLength + 1` |
+| 7 | Cmd Family | `0x0B` (Standard Control) |
+| 8+ | **Payload** | The raw command bytes. |
+
+### B. Checksum Calculation
+Applies to almost all raw payloads.
+- **Logic**: Sum all bytes in the raw payload and apply `& 0xFF` (modulo 256).
+
+---
+
+## 4. Command Library (Hex Level)
+
+### Power & Connectivity
+- **Power ON**: `[0x71, 0x23, 0x0F, 0xA3]`
+- **Power OFF**: `[0x71, 0x24, 0x0F, 0xA4]`
+- **Discovery**: Zengge devices typically broadcast as `LEDnetXXXXXX`.
+-   Direction Boolean: Byte [138] // (0x01 Forward, 0x00 Reverse)
+   Terminator: 0x0F
+   Checksum: sum(payload) & 0xFF
+
+=== ALTERNATIVE NON-ADDRESSABLE RGB PATTERNS (Node.js RAW DISCOVERIES) ===
+When pushing 0x42 packets, certain devices running generic non-IC LED firmware exhibit alternative mappings. Documenting these overrides here per user request for future legacy controller compatibility layers:
+- ID 56: Seven-Color Cross-Fade (Conflicts with our Symphony "Red Marquee")
+- ID 63: White Gradual Change
+- ID 64: Red/Green Cross-Fade
+- ID 67: Seven-Color Strobe Flash
+- ID 69: Green Strobe Flash
+- ID 76: Seven-Color Jumping Change
+* NOTE: The SK8Lytz system primarily targets Haloz / Soulz operating on WS2812B/SM16703 IC arrays, hence why these standard base-emitter mappings do not align mechanically with our SPI hardware.
+
+### Color & Brightness (`0x31`)
+- **Format**: `[0x31, R, G, B, 0x00, 0x00, 0x0F, Checksum]`
+- **Range**: `0x00` to `0xFF` (0-255).
+
+### RBM (Running Business Mode) (`0x42`)
+Modern high-performance pattern selection.
+- **Format**: `[0x42, PatternID, Speed, Brightness, Checksum]`
+- **Pattern IDs**: 1 - 100+ (See Master Pattern List).
+- **Default SK8Lytz Values**: Brightness 90% (`0x5A`), Speed 50% (`0x32`).
+
+### Addressable Mode (`0x59`) - Multi-Color Array / DIY Multi-Color
+- **Format**: `[0x59, SegmentLength, TransitionType, Speed, 0x01, R1,G1,B1, R2,G2,B2...]`
+- *Note on DIY Multi-Color Parity*: The Zengge APK's advanced "Multi-Color" tab natively utilizes this exact `0x59` chunked buffer to build DIY animations. The UI labels map strictly to these `TransitionType` bytes:
+  - `0x00`: **Static** (Color blocks sit still)
+  - `0x01`: **Gradual** (Flowing/Breathing transition)
+  - `0x02`: **Strobe** (Flashing segments)
+  - `0x03`: **Running Water** (Hard jumping Marquee)
+- **SegmentLength (Byte 1)** defines the size of the looping chunk. (Must be >=10 points to avoid hardware glitching).
+- **Speed (Byte 3)**: `0x01` (Slowest) to `0x64` (Fastest, usually bounded `0x20`+).
+- **Direction Boolean (Byte 138 - if length padded)**: `0x01` Forward flow, `0x00` Reverse flow.
+- A single 1-pixel padded string to `0x59` `Type 1` safely replicates Solid Mode without `0x31` flickering glitches.
+
+### Custom DIY Patterns (`0x51`)
+Unlimited creativity with up to 32 steps.
+- **Format**: `[0x51, Step1(8), Step2(8)... Step32(8), 0x0F, Checksum]`
+- **Step Payload**: `[Active(0xF0/0x0F), TransitionMode, Speed, R1, G1, B1, R2, G2, B2]`
+- **Transition Modes**: `0x3A` (Jump), `0x3B` (Gradual), `0x3C` (Strobe).
+
+---
+
+## 5. Fixed Modes Master List
+
+| ID | Name | Protocol | Logic / Hex Detail |
+|:---|:---|:---|:---|
+| 1 | **Solid** | `0x59` | Single perfectly-mapped pixel array `NumPoints=1`, `Speed>0` (req). |
+| 2 | **Single Dot** | `0x61` | `[FG, BG, BG, BG, BG, BG, BG, BG]` |
+| 3 | **Comet** | `0x61` | `[FG, 50%FG, 20%FG, BG, BG, BG]` |
+| 4 | **Dashed** | `0x61` | `[FG, FG, FG, FG, BG, BG, BG, BG]` |
+| 5 | **Alternating** | `0x61` | `[FG, FG, BG, BG]` |
+| 6 | **Breath** | `0x51` | 2-step `0x3B` Gradual Fade between FG and BG. |
+| 7 | **Flash** | `0x51` | 2-step `0x3A` Jump between FG and BG. |
+| 8 | **Strobe** | `0x51` | 2-step `0x3A` Jump at Speed 100. |
+| 9 | **Wave** | `0x61` | `[BG, BG, FG, FG, BG, BG]` Expansion. |
+| 10 | **Pinch** | `0x61` | `[FG, BG, BG, BG, BG, FG]` Contraction. |
+

+### Extended RBM / Symphony Modes (101-210)
+*These modes are undocumented in standard manuals but supported by the 0x42 protocol for addressable controllers.*
+
+| Range | Theme / Category | Visual Style |
+|:---|:---|:---|
+| `101-110` | **Prism Flow** | High-density multi-segment color flows (RGB, CMY, Pastel). |
+| `111-125` | **Neon Pulse** | Centered expansion and contraction with color shifting. |
+| `126-140` | **Star Field** | Randomized flickering with background color drifts. |
+| `141-160` | **Cyber Sprint** | One-way high-speed trails and "Shadow" effects. |
+| `161-175` | **Aurora Glow** | Soft, overlapping gradients moving at variable speeds. |
+| `176-190` | **Stack Matrix** | Stacking pixels with random colors at either end. |
+| `191-205` | **Festive Cycle** | Specialized loops for Christmas, Halloween, and New Years. |
+| `206-210` | **Zen Mode** | Ultra-slow "Breath" and "Deep Pulse" for sleeping/rest. |
+
+> [!TIP]
+> While SK8Lytz currently implements a curated list of the best 100 patterns, the protocol can trigger any of these 210 modes by sending the corresponding ID in the `0x42` command.
+
+> [!NOTE]
+> Pattern 100 has been redefined as **Emergency** mode.
+> - **Visuals**: Static Red (Heel), Static White (Toe), and **Bouncing** Yellow dots oscillating in the middle.
+> - **Protocol**: Uses `0x59` Segmented Flow to represent this custom layout on physical LEDs.
+

+## 9. UI Components & Iconography
+
+### Icons (MaterialCommunityIcons)
+- **Primary Branding**: `roller-skate`
+- **Main Interaction**: `power`
+- **Settings**: `tune` or `cog`
+
+### Group Visualization
+- **Single Device**: Single `roller-skate` icon (Size 22, `Colors.primary`).
+- **Grouped Devices**: Double `roller-skate` icons. The second icon is offset (`marginLeft: -10`) with reduced opacity (`0.8`) to create a stacked "pair" effect.
+
+---
+---
+
+## 10. Symphony Music Modes (Addressable)
+
+These modes are specific to Symphony controllers (HALOZ/SOULZ) using `ModeType 0x27`.
+
+### Mode Configuration (`0x73`)
+- **Format**: `[0x73, IsDeviceMic, 0x27, PatternID, R1, G1, B1, R2, G2, B2, Sensitivity, Brightness, Checksum]`
+### Pattern IDs & Reactive Logic (1-13)
+The `ProductVisualizer` mimics these behaviors using `audioMagnitude` (0.0 - 1.0) and `animValue` (Time-based loop).
+
+| ID | Name | Visual Behavior | Reactive Logic |
+|:---|:---|:---|:---|
+| 1 | **Soft** | Gentle pulsing. | `opacity = magnitude * (0.3 + 0.7 * h)` |
+| 2 | **Cheerful** | White sparkles on peaks. | `dotColor = (magnitude > 0.7) ? #FFF : color` |
+| 3 | **Energy** | Rapid color strobe. | `opacity = (magnitude > 0.5) ? 1.0 : 0.1` |
+| 4 | **Relax** | Slow color gradient. | `color = Interpolate(color, compHex)` |
+| 5 | **Passion** | Expansion from center. | `opacity = (mirroredFract < magnitude)` |
+| 6 | **Brisk** | Rhythmic jumping. | `opacity = (i % 2 == MagnitudeStep % 2)` |
+| 7 | **Rhythm** | VU Meter (Bottom-Up). | `opacity = (fract < magnitude)` |
+| 8 | **Rolling** | Color flow. | `opacity = magnitude` at anim position. |
+| 9 | **Flicker** | Random twinkling. | `opacity = (random < magnitude) ? 1.0 : 0.1` |
+| 10 | **Accumulation** | Edge-to-Center fill. | `opacity = (mirroredFract > (1 - magnitude))` |
+| 11 | **Shuttle** | Bouncing segments. | `opacity = magnitude` at anim position. |
+| 12 | **Fireworks** | Burst from center. | `burst = magnitude > 0.7` triggers flash. |
+| 13 | **Snow** | Falling white dots. | `opacity = magnitude` for falling segments. |
+
+## 10. App Microphone Live Sync (`0x74`)
+
+Used when `IsDeviceMic` is `0x00` in the `0x73` configuration.
+
+- **Command**: `[0x74, Magnitude, Checksum]`
+- **Magnitude**: `0x00` - `0xFF` (0-255) based on audio amplitude.
+- **Workflow**: 
+  1. Send `0x73` with `IsDeviceMic=0`.
+  2. Stream `0x74` every 50-100ms.
+  3. Send `0x73` with `IsDeviceMic=1` to return to hardware mic.
+
+---
+
+## 11. Advanced Reverse Engineering Observations
+
+The following details were extracted from `com.zengge.blev2` (Surplife) string resources and reflect advanced system behaviors.
+
+### Broadcast BLE Grouping Protocol
+Surplife uses a specialized "Broadcast" system for synchronized multi-device control.
+- **Data Table**: `broadcast_blue_network` (Columns: `id`, `network_id`).
+- **Logic**: Individual devices are assigned to a `broadcast_blue_network` to receive synchronous commands.
+- **Key Commands identified**:
+  - `createBroadcastBleGroupIfNotExist`
+  - `sendBroadcastDeviceGroupCommand`
+  - `loopSyncBroadcastBleDeviceGroup`
+- **Splicing Logic**: Symphony controllers support a "Splicing" setting to treat multiple physical strips as one continuous virtual strip. If splicing settings are inconsistent within a group, the app triggers a reset.
+
+### Group Leadership
+Large groups utilize a "Group Leader" logic to coordinate timing and pattern synchronization.
+- **Error Condition**: `Detects that the current group does not have a group leader.` (Indicates a failure in mesh/broadcast coordination).
+
+## 12. BLE Discovery & Identification (SPI/Symphony)
+
+To ensure only compatible addressable controllers are shown to the user, the app uses a multi-layered filtering strategy during the BLE scan.
+
+### A. Primary Identification (Manufacturer Data)
+The most reliable way to identify a Zengge SPI/Symphony controller is by inspecting the **Manufacturer Data** field in the advertisement packet.
+
+- **Offset**: Byte index 9.
+- **Symphony Code**: `0x33` (51) or `0xBF` (191).
+- **Logic**: If byte 9 is `0x33` or `0xBF`, the device is a Symphony-compatible addressable strip.
+
+### B. Secondary Identification (Name Prefixes)
+If manufacturer data is unavailable or the device is during first-time pairing, the following case-insensitive name prefixes are used:
+
+| Prefix | Description |
+|:---|:---|
+| `LEDnet` | Standard default Zengge factory name. |
+| `SK8` | Custom SK8Lytz branding. |
+| `ZG` | Zengge reference designs. |
+| `HALO` | SK8Lytz Halo variant. |
+| `SOUL` | SK8Lytz Soul variant. |
+
+### C. Service UUID Validation
+All compatible controllers SHOULD advertise the primary Service UUID:
+- `0000ffff-0000-1000-8000-00805f9b34fb`.
+
+---
+
+---
+
+## 13. Fixed Mode (Pattern 1-10) Implementation
+
+The "Fixed Mode" in the SK8Lytz app utilizes three distinct protocols to provide high-quality static and moving patterns on addressable hardware:
+
+### 1. Standard Solid (Pattern 1)
+- **Commands**: `0x59` (Segmented Multi-Color Repeating). Note: `0x51` produces 299-byte payloads crashing standard MTUs and freezing the app UI stack. To dynamically accommodate any LED point size without modulo remainders and avoid standard 0-speed hardware rejection, we force `NumPoints=1` mapped continuously with `Speed>0`.
+- **Behavior**: Sets all pixels to a single color.
+- **Reactivity**: Immediately updates on color picker or hue slider change.
+
+### 2. Symphony Multi-Color (Patterns 2-5, 9-10)
+- **Command**: `0x59`
+- **Logic**: Sends an array of colors that repeats or shifts based on the controller's internal logic.
+- **Pattern 2 (Single Dot)**: `[fg, bg, bg, bg, bg, bg, bg, bg]` (Repeating).
+- **Pattern 3 (Comet)**: `[fg, 50%fg, 20%fg, bg, bg, bg]` (Creates a fading tail effect).
+- **Pattern 4 (Dashed)**: `[fg, fg, fg, fg, bg, bg, bg, bg]` (4-pixel segments).
+- **Pattern 5 (Alternating)**: `[fg, fg, bg, bg]` (2-pixel segments).
+- **Pattern 9 (Wave)**: `[bg, bg, fg, fg, bg, bg]` (A moving 6-pixel wave).
+- **Pattern 10 (Pinch)**: `[fg, bg, bg, bg, bg, fg]` (Inward/Outward movement from edges).
+
+### 3. Custom Step Mode (Patterns 6-8)
+- **Command**: `0x51`
+- **Logic**: Defines a sequence of colors and a transition mode (Jump/Fade).
+- **Pattern 6 (Breath)**: Fade between `fg` and `bg`.
+- **Pattern 7 (Flash)**: Jump between `fg` and `bg`.
+- **Pattern 8 (Strobe)**: Fast jump between `fg` and `bg` with fixed speed.
+
+### 4. Street Mode (Accelerometer Reactive)
+- **Command**: `0x59`
+- **Logic**: Reads device telemetry from `expo-sensors` to detect sudden braking (negative G-forces / spatial Jerk calculations).
+- **Cruising State**: Generates an automotive frame mimicking running headlights and amber marker lights.
+- **Braking State**: Instantly forces a `#FF0000` (Red) high-priority override to emulate vehicle brake lights when physical deceleration thresholds are breached.
+
+## 14. App UI Iconography
+
+To maintain consistent branding and clarity, the app uses specific emojis for device and group identification in the Dashboard list.
+
+| Element | Icon | Logic |
+|:---|:---|:---|
+| **Individual Device** | `roller-skate` | `MaterialCommunityIcons`, 1 icon |
+| **Device Group** | `roller-skate` x2 | `MaterialCommunityIcons`, 2 icons (overlapping) |
+| **Device Name** | `SK8Lytz-****` | Fallback for factory names, using last 4 MAC digits. |
+| **RSSI Display** | `-XX dBm` | Displayed alongside MAC, "RSSI:" label removed. |
+| **Demo MACs** | `00:DE:M0:00:00:0X` | Realistic dummy format for IDs starting with `sim-`. |
+| **Pattern Wheel** | Circular | Looping logic (1 ├óΓÇáΓÇ¥ 100). |
+| **Pattern Hold** | 500ms Skip | Long-press auto-scroll triggers after 0.5s. |
+

+## 15. Zengge APK Reverse Engineering Findings (com.zengge.blev2)
+
+### A. App Architecture & Payload Construction
+1. **Hybrid Structure**: The Zengge app uses Flutter for all UI and business logic, while the native Android code acts as a BLE bridge.
+2. **Payload Origin**: The actual hex arrays mapping to commands like `0x42`, `0x51`, `0x59` are constructed inside the compiled AOT Dart code (`flutter_assets`), not native Java.
+3. **Native Bridge (`FlutterBleControl.java`)**: The Flutter layer passes complete byte payloads and configuration targets directly to native BLE write functions, meaning the native app simply transmits what Flutter computes.
+
+### B. Device State Mapping (`DeviceState2SymphonyLamp`)
+The native code tracks the state of connecting hardware using the following byte structure (tracked in a 14-byte `DeviceState` array):
+- **Red/Green/Blue**: Mapped to state positions `j`, `k`, `l`.
+- **HSV Settings (Symphony Lamps)**: 
+  - `Hue`: Stored natively as variable `t`.
+  - `Saturation`: Variable `w` (0-100).
+  - `Brightness/Value`: Variable `x` (0-100).
+- **Mode `0x97` (Static Color)**: Natively mapped from HSV settings to the RGB arrays during dynamic translations. When setting solid Symphony colors, the app defaults to mode `97` (decimal).
+
+### C. Device Controller Types (Native Offsets)
+- `Ctrl_Mini_RGB_Symphony_0xa1.java`: Handles 0xA1 control protocol types.
+- `Ctrl_RGBCW_Both_0x25.java`: RGBCW devices use the identifier `37` (0x25) and map brightness combinations between RGB diodes and White/Warm diodes to emulate exact CCT temperatures and luminosities natively.
+
+### D. Hardware IC Types & Discovery
+- Identified natively supported IC types inside the settings mappings (`SymphonyICTypeItem`):
+  1. `DIM` (1)
+  2. `CCT` (2)
+  3. `RGB` (3)
+  4. `RGB & W` (4)
+  5. `RGB & CCT` (5)
+  6. `RGB / W` (6)
+  7. `RGB / CCT` (7)
+These mappings closely relate to the `setHardwareConfig` (`0x81`) command values utilized in the `ZenggeProtocol.ts`.
+
+---
+*End of Master Reference. KEEP UPDATING ON ALL NEW FEATURES.*
+

+
+### CRITICAL HARDWARE FINDINGS (0x59 & Ambient Optics)
+1. **Array Length Glitching**: Continuously transmitting a 0x59 payload with an array length of < 10 causes the first chunk of physical LEDs to glitch and flicker severely. The array length MUST be dynamically padded to fall >= 10 to establish a perfectly solid, stable loop on the controller.
+2. **Matrix Transition State Locks**: The Symphony controller firmware natively ties `0x59` movement rules to the Transition Byte.
+    - **Type `0x00` (Static Flow)**: Instructs the array to cascade and naturally loop across the skateboard (used for Marquee, Comet, and Alternating).
+    - **Type `0x01` (Gradual)**: Systematically locks the array in place, freezing all internal gradients into an unmoving stream. This is required to prevent flickering on `Solid` pattern outputs.
+3. **Camera Optic Saturation Scaling**: Raw environment telemetry gathered from device cameras contains heavily desaturated hex codes due to fluorescent glare. To map properly to addressable strips, the hex matrix must be mathematically normalized by completely subtracting the noise floor (minimum RGB channel) and instantly scaling the dominant channel to `255`, ensuring pure structural saturation reaches the BLE pipeline.
+
+---
+
+## 6. Advanced V5 Firmware Discoveries (LedNetWF)
+*Discovered via HomeAssistant / LEDNetWF repository analysis against V5 microcontrollers.*
+
+### Candle Mode (Flicker Simulation)
+- The V5 firmware supports a native "Candle" effect that uses internal algorithms to realistically simulate a flickering flame.
+- **Parameters**: It allows specific adjustments for baseline brightness, flicker speed, and base RGB lighting color to establish warm ambient atmospheres completely independently of the static `0x42` pattern bounds.
+
+### Hardware Alarms & Timers
+- **Offline Schedules**: V5 controllers possess dedicated memory banks to store daily and weekly schedule masks (alarms) independently of the mobile app.
+- **Power & Action Triggers**: Hex arguments natively support `alarm-on` (Boot device), `alarm-off` (Kill power), `alarm-rgb` (Boot on specific Static Hex array), and `alarm-effect` (Boot into a specific Pattern ID).
+- **Known Firmware Glitch**: While writing alarms to device memory typically succeeds and populates correctly inside the official Zengge visual interfaces, the execution of "Repeat Day Masks" contains firmware-level race conditions that occasionally prevent the alarms from physically firing at the target time. OFF schedules possess definitively higher reliability than ON/Effect schedules.
+
+### Smear Payload Protocol (Raw Streaming Vectors)
+- The raw pixel-by-pixel color buffer stream utilized by certain V5 apps is classified as a "Smear Packet".
+- **Structure**: These are functionally massive variants of the `0x59` matrix mapped into 144-byte streams (48 pixels * 3 channels), containing dedicated bit flags for directional stream math (`1`=static, `2`=stream, `3`=strobe, `4`=jump).
+
+========================================================================
+             SECTION: HARDWARE STRIP IC & COLOR SEQUENCING
+                        (WS2812B / SM16703 PARITY)
+========================================================================
+
+## THE  x81 HARDWARE BOUNDARY PACKET
+Zengge BLE controllers do *not* require the controlling smartphone application to manually scramble RGB sequence bytes to match the target LEDs (e.g., swapping bytes to GRB natively in JS before Bluetooth transmission).
+
+Instead, the ecosystem relies on the **0x81 Configuration Command**. This command acts as a physical 'gateway setting' written directly into the controller's memory.**0x81 Format (SET Hardware Settings)**:
+The packet format requires exactly 6 parameters prefixed by the 0x81 header flag.
+NOTE: This structure changed based on deep protocol audits. Segments are definitively a single byte.
+[0x81, ICByte, OrderByte, PointsHigh, PointsLow, SegmentsByte, Checksum]
+
+- **ICByte**: Maps explicitly to the silicon driver type.
+  - WS2812B:  x01
+  - SM16703:  x02
+  - SM16704:  x03
+  - WS2811:  x04
+  - SK6812:  x05
+- **OrderByte**: Maps to the physical copper wiring layout of the LED diodes.
+  - RGB:  x00
+  - GRB:  x01 (Standard WS2812B)
+  - BRG:  x02
+
+## THE 0x63 / 0x0A HARDWARE RESPONSE PACKET (GET)
+When querying the controller (e.g. via 0x10), the response arrives with the full Zengge Header.
+The payload data starts at Index 7.
+
+- **Index 7**: Command Header (Usually 0x0A or 0x63 or 0x81)
+- **Index 8**: IC Type (`ICByte`)
+- **Index 9**: Color Sorting (`OrderByte`)
+- **Index 10**: Points High Byte
+- **Index 11**: Points Low Byte
+- **Index 12**: Segments Byte
+
+## 0x59 PAYLOAD DESERIALIZATION CAVEATS
+Because the hardware controller automatically unscrambles standard RGB packets based on the aforementioned  x81 config, all mobile app arrays (like  x59 running marquee multi-colors) MUST ALWAYS BE BROADCAST IN PURE R, G, B FORMAT. 
+
+If the React Native visualizer renders 'green' when 'red' is selected, this is strictly a mathematical index parsing error inside the UI code, *not* a requirement to artificially scramble the Bluetooth transmission payload.
+
+- **0x59 Structure Constraint**: The payload dynamic color string ALWAYS begins explicitly at **Index 3**.
+  - [0x59, LengthHigh, LengthLow, R1, G1, B1, R2, G2, B2...]
+- Reading visualizer chunks manually offset to Index 5 strictly induces a complete color channel phase shift (Reading B1 as R2, R2 as G2, etc). Always interpret colors starting directly after the LengthLow byte.
+
+========================================================================
+             SECTION: BLUETOOTH RSSI (SIGNAL STRENGTH) TOLERANCES
+========================================================================
+
+## BLUETOOTH LOW ENERGY (BLE) ATTENUATION SCALING
+The Sk8Lytz Dashboard actively measures physical Bluetooth Signal Attenuation (RSSI) expressed in negative decibel-milliwatts (dBm) natively translating to Wifi-style visual meters (`wifi-strength-X`).
+
+- **Excellent Quality (> -60 dBm)**: Direct Line-of-Sight, Minimal Interference. Packet streaming (0x59 Arrays / 0x31 Solid Matrix) will be completely structurally intact without frame shedding.
+  - UI Visualization: `Green` | `wifi-strength-4`
+
+- **Fair Quality (-61 dBm to -80 dBm)**: Distanced Connection / Minor Physical Occlusion (i.e. Body Blocking). Array streaming will occasionally delay response by 50ms-150ms.
+  - UI Visualization: `Orange` | `wifi-strength-2`
+
+- **Poor Quality (< -80 dBm)**: Extreme Attenuation / High Interference. Native physical controller packet drops will occur gracefully causing intermittent visually skipping frames or missing firmware overrides.
+  - UI Visualization: `Red` | `wifi-strength-1`
+
+- **Unknown / Booting (0 or Null)**: Connecting phase resolving physical connection states.
+  - UI Visualization: `Grey` | `wifi-strength-outline`
+
+========================================================================
+             SECTION: NATIVE UI ARCHITECTURE
+========================================================================
+
+## ACTIVE CONTROLLER COMPONENTS
+The application now exclusively relies on `DockedController.tsx` for all unified controller UI overlays, deprecating and permanently removing `ModernController.tsx` to maintain feature parity without conflicting state trees.
+
+## SCANNER MODULE DIMENSIONS
+The `ScannerAnimation.tsx` projection wrapper inside the DOM natively sits at `380px` height constraints, preventing the sweeping MAX_RADIUS = 280 (560px diameter) sonar rings from vertically clipping, significantly enhancing the visual impact of the BLE pairing screen natively.
+
+## FIXED PATTERN TIER LIST
+The physical array list for "Solid Patterns" is locked at 10 native fixed iterations mapping directly to internal protocol handlers. (1: Solid, 2: Single Dot ... 10: Pinch).
+
+========================================================================
+         SECTION: HARDWARE SETTINGS DEEP REVERSE ENGINEERING
+             (From APK Decompile - April 2026 Audit)
+         Source Files: SymphonySettingForA3.java, tc/b.java, dd/i.java
+========================================================================
+
+## 16. Hardware Settings Protocol (Complete Specification)
+
+This section documents the COMPLETE BLE protocol for reading and writing
+all hardware settings for Zengge Symphony addressable LED controllers
+(HALOZ / SOULZ), as extracted from decompiled `com.zengge.blev2` APK v1.5.0.
+
+---
+
+### A. QUERY COMMAND: Read Current Hardware Settings (0x63 / command byte 99)
+
+The Zengge app sends a 5-byte query packet to request the current hardware
+configuration from the device. This is sent once immediately on connection.
+
+**Source**: `tc/b.java ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ public static byte[] f0(boolean z10)`
+
+```
+QUERY PACKET FORMAT (5 bytes raw, before V2 wrapper):
+  bArr[0] = 0x63  (99)   // Opcode: "get hardware config"
+  bArr[1] = 0x12  (18)   // Sub-command identifier
+  bArr[2] = 0x21  (33)   // Sub-command parameter (0x21 = query mode)
+  bArr[3] = 0xF0  (240)  // 0xF0 if device has mic, 0x0F if not
+  bArr[4] = checksum(bArr, 4)
+```
+
+**When to send**: Immediately after BLE connection established, before sending
+any pattern or config commands.
+
+---
+
+### B. RESPONSE PACKET: Hardware Settings Reply (opcode 0x63 / 99 in position [0])
+
+**Source**: `tc/b.java ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ static class a ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ public static SymphonyICTypeItem g(byte[] bArr)`
+
+The device responds with a 12-byte packet. Validation: `bArr[0] == 99` AND
+`bArr[11] == checksum(bArr, 11)`.
+
+```
+RESPONSE PACKET FORMAT (12 bytes):
+  bArr[0]  = 0x63  (99)   // Response opcode (matches query opcode)
+  bArr[1]  = ??           // Sub-type byte (ignored in parsing)
+  bArr[2]  = ??           // Ignored
+  bArr[3]  = ICType       // Strip Type / IC Wiring Type (0-based index)
+  bArr[4]  = ICParam_c    // IC timing param c (T0H in ns)
+  bArr[5]  = ICParam_d    // IC timing param d (T0L in ns)
+  bArr[6]  = ICParam_e    // IC timing param e (T1H in ns)
+  bArr[7]  = ICParam_f    // IC timing param f (T1L in ns)
+  bArr[8]  = Points_High  // LED Points High Byte (big-endian with [9])
+  bArr[9]  = Points_Low   // LED Points Low Byte
+  bArr[10] = ColorSorting // Color order index (see Sorting Table below)
+  bArr[11] = Checksum     // sum(bArr[0..10]) & 0xFF
+```
+
+**Parsing LED Points (total count)**:
+```javascript
+ledPoints = ((bArr[9] & 0xFF) << 8) | (bArr[8] & 0xFF)
+// NOTE: bytes are SWAPPED - g2.c.a(new byte[]{bArr[9], bArr[8]})
+// meaning bArr[8]=Low, bArr[9]=High (little-endian pair in that field)
+```
+
+**Parsing IC Type**: `bArr[3] & 0xFF` ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ lookup in IC Type Table
+**Parsing Color Sorting**: `bArr[10] & 0xFF` ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ lookup in Sorting Table
+
+---
+
+### C. WRITE COMMAND: Set Hardware Settings (opcode 0x62 / 98)
+
+**Source**: `tc/b.java ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ public static byte[] C(int i10, int i11, int i12, int i13, int i14, int i15)`
+
+The full 11-byte set-hardware-config command (before V2 wrapper):
+
+```
+WRITE PACKET FORMAT (11 bytes):
+  bArr[0]  = 0x62  (98)   // Opcode: "set hardware config"
+  bArr[1]  = Points_High  // LED Points High byte (g2.c.c(points)[1])
+  bArr[2]  = Points_Low   // LED Points Low byte  (g2.c.c(points)[0])
+  bArr[3]  = Seg_High     // LED Segments High byte (g2.c.c(segments)[1])
+  bArr[4]  = Seg_Low      // LED Segments Low byte  (g2.c.c(segments)[0])
+  bArr[5]  = ICType       // Strip Type index (see IC Type Table)
+  bArr[6]  = ColorSorting // Color order index (see Sorting Table)
+  bArr[7]  = MicPoints    // Points for music mode  (for Symphony mic)
+  bArr[8]  = MicSegments  // Segments for music mode
+  bArr[9]  = 0xF0  (-16)  // Fixed terminator byte
+  bArr[10] = checksum(bArr, 10)
+```
+
+**Parameter constraints (from SymphonySettingForA3.java)**:
+- `ledPoints` (f24921l): 1 to 300 max. Constraint: points * segments <= 2048.
+- `ledSegments` (f24922m): 1 to (2048 / ledPoints) max.
+- `micPoints` (f24923n): 1 to 150 max. Constraint: micPoints * micSegments <= 960.
+- `micSegments` (f24924p): 1 to (960 / micPoints) max.
+- Default fallback if zeros detected: points=30, segments=10.
+
+---
+
+### D. IC TYPE TABLE (Strip Type / "Wiring Type")
+
+**Source**: `dd/i.java ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ public static ArrayList<SymphonyICTypeItem> m(boolean z10, int i10)`
+
+This is the complete list for the A3/A2 controller (our HALOZ/SOULZ hardware).
+The `ICType` byte in the packet corresponds to the index value (field `f23990a`).
+
+For non-mic mode (z10=false, which is our use case):
+
+| Index | Name        | T0H | T0L | T1H | T1L | MaxHz |
+|-------|-------------|-----|-----|-----|-----|-------|
+|   1   | WS2812B     |  14 |  12 |   6 |  18 | 1000  |
+|   2   | SM16703     |  18 |   6 |   0 |  18 | 1600  |
+|   3   | SM16704     |  18 |   6 |   0 |  18 | 1600  |
+|   4   | WS2811      |  40 |  10 |  10 |  40 | 1000  |
+|   5   | UCS1903     |  40 |  10 |  10 |  40 |  480  |
+|   6   | SK6812      |  12 |  12 |   6 | 900 | 1600  |
+|   7   | SK6812RGBW  |  12 |  12 |   6 | 900 | 1600  |
+|   8   | INK1003     |  12 |  12 |   6 | 900 | 1600  |
+|   9   | UCS2904B    |  12 |  12 |   6 | 900 | 1600  |
+|  10   | JY1903      |  12 |  12 |   6 | 900 | 1600  | (firmware >= 2)
+|  11   | WS2812E     |  12 |  12 |   6 | 900 | 1600  | (firmware >= 3)
+
+**SK8Lytz Default**: Index 1 = WS2812B (HALOZ) or Index 2 = SM16703 (SOULZ)
+
+---
+
+### E. COLOR SORTING TABLE (Strip Type Ordering)
+
+**Source**: `SymphonySettingForA3.java ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ b1() method`
+
+Color sorting index values used in both query response byte[10] and write
+command byte[6]:
+
+For standard RGB strips (non-RGBW):
+| Index | Name |
+|-------|------|
+|   0   | RGB  |
+|   1   | RBG  |
+|   2   | GRB  |
+|   3   | GBR  |
+|   4   | BRG  |
+|   5   | BGR  |
+
+For RGBW strips (ICType 7 = SK6812RGBW):
+| Index | Name |
+|-------|------|
+|   0   | RGBW |
+|   1   | RBGW |
+|   2   | GRBW |
+|   3   | GBRW |
+|   4   | BRGW |
+|   5   | BGRW |
+|   6   | WRGB |
+|   7   | WRBG |
+|   8   | WGRB |
+|   9   | WGBR |
+|  10   | WBRG |
+|  11   | WBGR |
+
+**SK8Lytz Default**: Index 2 = GRB (standard WS2812B wiring)
+
+NOTE: The original 0x81 command used a 1-based color order (RGB=1, GRB=3).
+The new 0x63/0x62 protocol uses 0-based indexing (RGB=0, GRB=2). These
+are equivalent but the offset differs. Always use 0-based for new protocol.
+
+---
+
+### F. FIRMWARE VERSION DETECTION
+
+**Source**: `ZGHBDevice.java` (advertisement packet parsing)
+
+Firmware version is embedded in the BLE manufacturer advertisement data,
+NOT via a BLE command. It is read during scan/discovery:
+
+```
+Manufacturer data byte layout (29-byte payload at AD type 0xFF):
+  bArr[0]  = State byte (STA)
+  bArr[1..2] = Manufacturer ID (big-endian)
+  bArr[3]  = BLE Protocol Version (bleVersion)
+  bArr[4..9] = MAC address (6 bytes)
+  bArr[10..11] = Product ID (big-endian uint16)
+  bArr[12] = Firmware Version (low byte = firmwareVer & 0xFF)
+  bArr[13] = LED Version (ledVersion & 0xFF)
+  bArr[14] = Additional flags (checkKeyFlag & 0x03, ext firmwareVer bits)
+  bArr[15] = firmwareFlag (& 0x1F)
+  bArr[16..26] = State array (11 bytes for bleVersion < 7)
+```
+
+**firmwareVer full value formula** (for bleVersion >= 6):
+```javascript
+firmwareVer = (bArr[12] & 0xFF) | (((bArr[14] & 0xFFFF) >> 2) << 8)
+```
+
+For bleVersion < 6:
+```javascript
+firmwareVer = bArr[12] & 0xFF
+```
+
+**ledVersion**: `bArr[13] & 0xFF` (separate from firmwareVer)
+
+**Manufacturer IDs (valid ranges)**:
+- 23123-23133 (exact)
+- 23072-23087 (range)
+- 23136-23151 (range)
+- 23152-23167 (range)
+- 23168-23183 (range)
+
+---
+
+### G. LED SEGMENTS EXPLAINED
+
+The `ledSegments` field (f24922m in APK) represents the number of LED
+"segment groups" the controller treats as a logical unit. This is distinct
+from `ledPoints`:
+
+- **ledPoints**: Individual LED pixel count per segment.
+- **ledSegments**: How many of those segments are chained.
+- **Total LEDs**: `ledPoints ├âΓÇö ledSegments` (max 2048).
+
+For SK8Lytz HALOZ (16 LEDs): points=16, segments=1 ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ total=16
+For SK8Lytz SOULZ (43 LEDs): points=43, segments=1 ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ total=43
+
+The Zengge settings UI displays: "Points", "Segments", and "Sum" (= P ├âΓÇö S).
+
+---
+
+### H. FULL ROUND-TRIP WORKFLOW (On Connection)
+
+1. **BLE connection established** to device.
+2. **Send query**: `f0(hasMic)` ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ `[0x63, 0x12, 0x21, 0xF0|0x0F, checksum]`
+   - Wrap in V2 packet wrapper before sending.
+3. **Await 12-byte response** starting with `bArr[0] == 0x63`.
+4. **Parse response**:
+   - `icType = bArr[3] & 0xFF`
+   - `icParamC = bArr[4] & 0xFF` (T0H)
+   - `icParamD = bArr[5] & 0xFF` (T0L)
+   - `icParamE = bArr[6] & 0xFF` (T1H)
+   - `icParamF = bArr[7] & 0xFF` (T1L)
+   - `ledPoints = g2.c.a([bArr[9], bArr[8]])` ├óΓÇá┬É low/high SWAPPED
+   - `colorSorting = bArr[10] & 0xFF`
+5. **Look up IC name** from IC Type Table using `icType` index.
+6. **Look up color order name** from Sorting Table using `colorSorting`.
+7. **Update UI** with detected values.
+8. **Store in `ng_device_configs`** AsyncStorage per device MAC.
+9. **Optionally re-send** `0x81` hardware config to confirm alignment.
+
+---
+
+### I. WRITE HARDWARE SETTINGS WORKFLOW
+
+When user changes settings in Hardware Settings UI and confirms:
+
+1. Build write packet via C(points, segments, icType, sorting, micPts, micSegs).
+2. Send 11-byte packet (V2 wrapped) to device.
+3. Device applies and persists the configuration.
+4. Optionally re-query (step 2 above) to confirm round-trip.
+5. Update `ng_device_configs` cache.
+
+---
+
+### J. EXISTING 0x81 COMMAND RELATIONSHIP
+
+The existing `0x81` command in our codebase is a LEGACY format that is
+functionally replaced by the `0x62`/`0x63` pair:
+
+| Feature | 0x81 (legacy) | 0x62/0x63 (new) |
+|---------|---------------|-----------------|
+| Query   | No            | Yes (0x63)      |
+| Write   | Yes           | Yes (0x62)      |
+| Points  | Yes           | Yes             |
+| Segments| No            | Yes             |
+| IC Type | Partial       | Full IC table   |
+| Mic settings | No     | Yes             |
+
+The 0x81 command continues to work for basic configuration but the 0x62/0x63
+protocol should be used for the full hardware settings dialog.
+
+---
+
+*End of Hardware Settings Deep Reverse Engineering Section ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ April 2026*
+

+A. FILES MODIFIED

+1. src/protocols/ZenggeProtocol.ts  (COMPLETE REWRITE)
+   - queryHardwareSettings(hasMic)
+       Builds correct 5-byte query: [0x63, 0x12, 0x21, 0x0F, checksum]
+       Source: tc/b.java ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ f0(boolean)
+
+   - parseHardwareSettingsResponse(raw)
+       Parses 12-byte response from device.
+       CRITICAL BYTE SWAP: ledPoints = (bytes[9] << 8) | bytes[8]
+         (little-endian pair, NOT big-endian as one might assume)
+       Validates checksum: sum(bytes[0..10]) & 0xFF == bytes[11]
+       Handles both raw (starts 0x63) and V2-wrapped (8-byte header) responses.
+
+   - writeHardwareSettings(points, segments, icType, sorting, micPts?, micSegs?)
+       Builds correct 11-byte write: [0x62, ptsHi, ptsLo, segHi, segLo,
+         icType, sorting, micPts, micSegs, 0xF0, checksum]
+       Source: tc/b.java ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ C(int, int, int, int, int, int)
+
+   - parseFirmwareFromAdvertisement(base64)
+       Extracts firmware version from BLE scan advertisement manufacturer data.
+       Source: ZGHBDevice.java ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ setDeviceInfo(byte[])
+       Bytes: [12] = fw low, [14] >> 2 = fw high (when bleVersion >= 6)
+
+   - HardwareSettings interface: ledPoints, segments, icType, icName,
+       colorSorting, colorSortingName, firmwareVer, detected
+
+   - SK8_DEFAULTS constants:
+       HALOZ: { points: 16, segments: 1, icType: 1 (WS2812B), sorting: 2 (GRB) }
+       SOULZ: { points: 43, segments: 1, icType: 2 (SM16703), sorting: 2 (GRB) }
+
+   - HW_CONSTRAINTS: maxPoints=300, maxPxS=2048, maxMicPoints=150, maxMicPxS=960
+

+   - QUERY button per device ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ sends 0x63, waits up to 5s for response
+   - QUERY ALL button ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ sequential query of all visible devices

+D. KNOWN CONSTRAINTS & DESIGN DECISIONS
+--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
+
+  - Segments NOT returned in 0x63 response ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ managed as local state, defaults to 1
+  - All LED point parsing uses little-endian byte swap: (bytes[9]<<8)|bytes[8]
+  - 0x62/0x63 pair deprecates 0x81 for hardware settings (0x81 kept for compat)
+  - Firmware version extracted from BLE advertisement, NOT via command
+  - maxPoints x maxSegments must not exceed 2048 (enforced in writeHardwareSettings)
+  - setOnDataReceived prop required in Sk8LytzProgrammerModal to capture 0x63 responses

+*Last Updated: April 2026*
+  
+## 20. Hardware Synchronization & Points/Segments  
+- Physical Segments: Act as multipliers for standard paths. Applications must bounds clamp raw array payloads matching exactly Math.floor(pts / segments) to prevent overflow tearing across repeating bounds on V2 Symphony hardware.  
+- Color Sorting Constraints: Array generation, music UI mode secondary/primary mapping, and fixed arrays rely natively on ZenggeProtocol.applyColorSorting to enforce user configuration explicitly at payload creation. 
+
+
+---
+
+## 21. CODEBASE ARCHITECTURE ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ COMPLETE FILE REFERENCE
+
+*Last Updated: April 5, 2026. DO NOT SHORTEN THIS SECTION.*
+
+This section documents every source file in the SK8Lytz application: what it is, what it does, why it is necessary, when it runs, and how it connects to everything else.
+
+---
+
+### A. ENTRY POINTS & ROOT CONFIG
+
+**`index.ts`** (root)
+- The React Native app entry point. Registers the root App component with Expo's AppRegistry.
+- **Why**: Required by React Native's module resolver to bootstrap the application on device.
+- **When**: Executed once at cold launch by the native Android/iOS runtime.
+
+**`App.tsx`** (root)
+- Wraps the entire application in the `ThemeContext.Provider` to make light/dark theme state globally available.
+- Renders `DashboardScreen` as the sole top-level screen ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ this app has no navigator.
+- **Why**: Single-screen app architecture keeps performance lean for BLE-intensive operations.
+- **When**: Mounted immediately after `index.ts` and remains alive for the entire app lifetime.
+
+**`app.json` / `app.config.js`** (root)
+- Expo configuration: app name, icon, splash screen, Android permissions (BLUETOOTH_SCAN, BLUETOOTH_CONNECT, ACCESS_FINE_LOCATION), and bundle identifier.
+- **Why**: Android requires explicit manifest-level permission declarations for BLE access. Missing even one breaks scanning on API 31+.
+
+**`android/`** (directory)
+- Native Android Gradle project generated by Expo's prebuild system.
+- **Why**: Required to produce an installable APK. The `build.gradle` files here configure signing, ProGuard, and native library resolution.
+- **Key file**: `android/app/build.gradle` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ release signing config, version code, and native dependency resolution.
+
+**`tools/build-apk.ps1`** and **`tools/install-on-device.ps1`**
+- PowerShell scripts that wrap `./gradlew assembleRelease` and `adb install` for one-command build + deploy.
+- **Why**: Removes the need to remember Gradle flags and ADB paths during rapid iteration cycles.
+- **When**: Manually invoked by the developer.
+
+---
+
+### B. SCREENS (`src/screens/`)
+
+**`DashboardScreen.tsx`** ├óΓÇá┬É *The application's entire UI lives here*
+- **Role**: The single root screen. Owns ALL top-level application state.
+- **What it manages**:
+  - BLE lifecycle: scan, connect, disconnect, multi-device group sync
+  - Device roster: `allDevices` (discovered), `connectedDevices` (active GATT connections)
+  - Custom groups: `customGroups` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ user-saved multi-device groups with name + member list
+  - Device configs: `deviceConfigs` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ per-device settings (name, type, LED points, segments, sorting, strip type) loaded from `ng_device_configs` in AsyncStorage
+  - Power states: per-device on/off boolean map
+  - UI modal visibility flags: settings panel, group builder, analytics, hardware tester, programmer
+  - BLE write dispatch: `writeToDevice()` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ routes commands to specific devices or all connected
+- **Key functions**:
+  - `saveSettings()` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ persists hardware config and fires `HARDWARE_CONFIG_CHANGED` + `DEVICE_RENAMED` audit events
+  - `saveGroup()` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ creates or updates a custom device group
+  - `handleGlobalPowerToggle()` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ sends power ON/OFF to a set of device IDs
+  - `openDeviceSettings()` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ triggers a 0x63 hardware query on the target device before opening the settings modal
+- **AsyncStorage keys it owns**:
+  - `ng_device_configs` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ dict keyed by MAC address, contains { name, type, points, segments, sorting, stripType, groupId }
+  - `ng_custom_groups` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ array of { id, name, isGroup, deviceIds }
+  - `ng_processed_devices` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ cached list of previously seen devices
+- **Why it's massive (61KB)**: Deliberately monolithic. BLE state cannot safely be split across components without introducing race conditions between connection events and UI re-renders. All hardware-touching logic must be co-located.
+- **When it runs**: Active from app open to close. Never unmounted.
+
+---
+
+### C. HOOKS (`src/hooks/`)
+
+**`useBLE.ts`** ├óΓÇá┬É *The Bluetooth engine*
+- **Role**: All BLE hardware interactions. Wraps `react-native-ble-plx`.
+- **What it exposes**:
+  - `scanForPeripherals()` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ starts a 5-second BLE scan. Applies strict filtering: only accepts devices that are Symphony-type (manufacturer byte 9 = 0x33/0xBF), have a known name prefix (lednet/sk8/zg/halo/soul), or advertise the Zengge service UUID. Logs `DEVICE_DISCOVERED` or `SCAN_FILTER_REJECT` for every candidate.
+  - `connectToDevice(device)` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ connects to a single device, discovers GATT services, starts characteristic monitoring for RX notifications, and attempts firmware read from both advertisement data and GATT 0x180A/0x2A26. Logs `DEVICE_CONNECTED` + `PERFORMANCE_METRIC` (latency).
+  - `connectToDevices(devices[])` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ sequential (NOT parallel) connection loop for group sync. Android GATT 133 errors occur if connections are attempted concurrently with `Promise.all`. Must be one-by-one.
+  - `writeToDevice(payload, targetDeviceId?)` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ encodes payload to base64, writes to `ZENGGE_CHARACTERISTIC_UUID`. If `targetDeviceId` is given, sends only to that device. Otherwise broadcasts to all connected.
+  - `disconnectFromDevice()` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ cancels all active GATT connections.
+- **Why it's a hook**: React's rendering lifecycle must track `connectedDevices` and `allDevices` as reactive state. Hooks allow BLE events to trigger re-renders cleanly.
+- **When it runs**: Instantiated once in `DashboardScreen` and never recreated. The `useMemo` return value is stable across re-renders.
+- **Critical design note**: `connectToDevices` uses a `for...of` sequential loop by design. Do NOT refactor to `Promise.all` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ this causes GATT 133 errors on Android.
+
+---
+
+### D. PROTOCOLS (`src/protocols/`)
+
+**`ZenggeProtocol.ts`** ├óΓÇá┬É *The hardware communication specification*
+- **Role**: Single source of truth for all BLE command payloads. Every byte sent to Zengge LED controllers is generated here.
+- **Key exports**:
+  - `ZENGGE_SERVICE_UUID` / `ZENGGE_CHARACTERISTIC_UUID` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ BLE GATT addresses for all read/write operations
+  - `IC_TYPES` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ map of IC chip indices (1-11) to names (WS2812B, SM16703, etc.)
+  - `COLOR_SORTING_RGB` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ map of color order indices (0-5) to names (RGB, GRB, etc.)
+  - `SK8_DEFAULTS` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ factory defaults for HALOZ (16L, WS2812B, GRB) and SOULZ (43L, SM16703, GRB)
+  - `HW_CONSTRAINTS` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ max points (300), max PxS (2048), mic constraints
+  - `wrapCommand(raw)` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ applies the 8-byte V2 packet header (seq counter, length, 0x0B family)
+  - `calculateChecksum(payload)` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ sum & 0xFF
+  - `queryHardwareSettings()` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ builds 0x63 query (5 bytes) to read EEPROM config from device
+  - `queryHardwareConfig()` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ alias for queryHardwareSettings, used in some call sites
+  - `parseHardwareSettingsResponse(data)` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ decodes the 12-byte 0x63 response: extracts IC type, color sorting, LED points (little-endian swapped bytes 8+9)
+  - `writeHardwareSettings(points, segs, icType, sorting)` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ builds 0x62 EEPROM write command
+  - `parseFirmwareFromAdvertisement(base64)` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ decodes firmware version from BLE scan advertisement manufacturer data
+  - `solidColor(r,g,b)` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ 0x31 fixed color command
+  - `rbmPattern(id)` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ 0x42 pattern selection (1-210)
+  - `musicMode(id)` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ music sync mode selection
+  - `cameraMode(id)` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ camera light tracking mode
+  - `power(on)` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ 0x71 power on/off
+  - `setBrightness(pct)` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ brightness 0-100
+  - `setSpeed(pct)` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ effect speed 0-100
+  - `applyColorSorting(r,g,b, sortingIndex)` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ remaps RGB values to the hardware's expected color channel order
+- **Why it's separate**: Protocol logic is completely hardware-specific with no React dependencies. Isolating it enables unit testing and reuse in admin/debug tools.
+- **When it runs**: Called any time a command needs to be sent ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ from `DockedController`, `DeviceSettingsModal`, `AdminHardwareTester`, and `Sk8LytzProgrammerModal`.
+
+---
+
+### E. SERVICES (`src/services/`)
+
+**`AppLogger.ts`** ├óΓÇá┬É *The analytics and telemetry engine*
+- **Role**: Captures all significant application events and uploads them to Supabase for remote analytics.
+- **Design**: Singleton exported as `AppLogger` (instance of `AppLoggerService`). Never instantiated twice.
+- **Local buffer**: Events are stored in a compact `LogEntry[]` array (`{ t: timestamp, e: EventType, d: payload }`). Buffer is persisted to AsyncStorage key `@sk8lytz_logs` and rotates at 10,000 entries.
+- **Event types logged**: `APP_OPENED`, `DEVICE_DISCOVERED`, `DEVICE_CONNECTED`, `DEVICE_DISCONNECTED`, `DEVICE_RENAMED`, `MODE_CHANGED`, `PATTERN_CHANGED`, `COLOR_CHANGED`, `BRIGHTNESS_CHANGED`, `SPEED_CHANGED`, `HARDWARE_CONFIG_CHANGED`, `SCAN_STARTED/COMPLETED/FILTER_MATCH/REJECT`, `BLE_WRITE_ERROR`, `BLE_CONNECTION_ERROR`, `PROTOCOL_ERROR`, `RAW_PAYLOAD` (hardware tester only), `SCREEN_OPENED`, `PERFORMANCE_METRIC`
+- **`uploadLogsToSupabase()`** ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ the main upload function. On success:
+  1. Merges with any existing cloud JSON in `sk8lytz-logs` Storage bucket (deduplicates by `t+e` fingerprint, excludes `RAW_PAYLOAD`)
+  2. Uploads merged JSON back to Storage
+  3. Runs the **Enterprise DB Injection Stream**: pushes current delta to 6 normalized Postgres tables
+  4. **Clears local buffer** after confirmed successful Postgres push (rotation)
+- **Custom device name resolution**: Reads `ng_device_configs` from AsyncStorage (same key `DashboardScreen` writes), builds a `customNameMap` keyed by device MAC, and injects the custom name into all Supabase row payloads.
+- **Session ID**: A single `sessionId` (`telemetry_TIMESTAMP`) is generated at singleton instantiation and reused for the entire app lifetime session ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ prevents duplicate session stats/device rows on repeated uploads via Upsert constraints.
+- **Supabase tables written**:
+  - `parsed_session_stats` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ one row per session (upserted on `session_id`)
+  - `parsed_session_devices` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ one row per device per session (upserted on `session_id, device_id`)
+  - `parsed_mode_usage` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ mode change frequency per device (group events unrolled per device)
+  - `parsed_pattern_usage` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ pattern selection frequency per device
+  - `parsed_color_usage` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ color selection frequency per device
+  - `parsed_logs` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ full event trace (group events flatMapped per device)
+- **Why `RAW_PAYLOAD` is excluded**: Raw BLE hex dumps are for the hardware tester terminal only. Including them in the analytics stream would generate millions of low-value rows and degrade query performance.
+- **When it runs**: `AppLogger.log()` is called synchronously throughout the app. `uploadLogsToSupabase()` is triggered manually or on app background.
+
+**`supabaseClient.ts`**
+- **Role**: Instantiates and exports the Supabase JS client using env vars (`EXPO_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL`, `EXPO_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY`).
+- **Why separate**: Supabase client initialization is expensive and must be a singleton. Both `AppLogger` and any future direct DB calls import from here.
+- **When it runs**: Initialized once at module load time, before any component renders.
+
+---
+
+### F. COMPONENTS (`src/components/`)
+
+**`DockedController.tsx`** ├óΓÇá┬É *The primary user control interface (125KB)*
+- **Role**: The full-featured LED control panel. Renders as a slide-up sheet docked to the bottom of the screen.
+- **What it controls**: Mode switching (Fixed, Music, Camera, Pattern, etc.), color picker and RGB sliders, brightness/speed knobs, pattern wheel, music visualizer EQ, DIY array builder, favorites system, quick presets, power toggle.
+- **Analytics**: Builds `deviceContext` (single device or group with `deviceIds` array) and logs `MODE_CHANGED`, `PATTERN_CHANGED`, `COLOR_CHANGED` with the full target context. Group events include the complete `deviceIds` array so the telemetry engine can unroll them.
+- **Why it's huge**: Every UI control mode (10+ modes) has its own internal sub-state. Splitting into sub-components risks prop-drilling BLE write callbacks 5+ levels deep.
+
+**`AdminHardwareTester.tsx`** ├óΓÇá┬É *The developer/admin diagnostic tool*
+- **Role**: Hidden admin panel for BLE packet inspection, payload generation, and EEPROM configuration. Accessible via secret gesture in DashboardScreen.
+- **Tabs**:
+  - **SNIFFER**: Live RX/TX BLE packet timeline. Parses 0x63 hardware responses and 0x81 status pings in real-time. Logs `RAW_PAYLOAD` events (the only place this event type is written).
+  - **FACTORY**: Payload generator for any Zengge command type (Solid, RBM, Music, Camera, Custom hex). Can fire directly to hardware.
+  - **CONFIG**: EEPROM configurator ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ shows current hardware settings, validates constraints, and writes 0x62 burn commands to device.
+- **Why separate from DockedController**: Admin tools must not be accessible to end users. The separate component allows it to be gated behind an undocumented activation pattern.
+- **When it runs**: Rendered only when the admin modal is open. Not mounted at app start.
+
+**`DeviceSettingsModal.tsx`**
+- **Role**: Per-device settings modal. User can rename a device, assign it to a group, set LED type, configure points/segments/sorting.
+- **Triggers**: Opening this modal automatically sends a 0x63 hardware query to read current EEPROM state into the form.
+- **Saves to**: `ng_device_configs` AsyncStorage key (same as what AppLogger reads for name resolution).
+- **Fires**: `HARDWARE_CONFIG_CHANGED` and `DEVICE_RENAMED` telemetry events on save.
+
+**`LogViewerModal.tsx`** ├óΓÇá┬É *The SK8Lytz Analytics viewer*
+- **Role**: In-app analytics dashboard. Reads from the local AppLogger buffer.
+- **Tabs**: LOGS timeline (virtualized, newest first), STATS (mode/pattern/color usage charts), DEVICES (all seen devices with config info), EXPORT (JSON dump trigger).
+- **Event map**: Maps every `EventType` to an icon, color, and label for display.
+- **Why local-only**: The analytics viewer shows the current device's session data. Historical cross-device data requires a future Supabase query endpoint (currently append-only, no SELECT policy for anon role).
+
+**`Sk8LytzProgrammerModal.tsx`** ├óΓÇá┬É *The hardware burn programmer*
+- **Role**: EEPROM programmer for batch hardware configuration. Scans visible devices, queries their current settings via 0x63, and writes new settings via 0x62.
+- **Cache key**: `@sk8_hw_<deviceId>` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ separate from `ng_device_configs` (device display settings vs hardware EEPROM settings).
+- **Why separate from DeviceSettingsModal**: The programmer targets raw hardware at protocol level. The DeviceSettingsModal is for end-user name/group/display management.
+
+**`ProductVisualizer.tsx`**
+- **Role**: Real-time LED simulation canvas. Renders a visual preview of the current color/pattern/mode on a diagram of the skate (HALOZ wheel ring, SOULZ sole strip).
+- **Why**: Provides immediate visual feedback without requiring physical hardware to be connected. Critical for demo/development mode.
+
+**`ScannerAnimation.tsx`**
+- **Role**: Animated BLE scanning UI shown during device discovery. Radar sweep animation with discovered device nodes appearing in real-time.
+- **When**: Mounted during `isScanning === true`.
+
+**`ArcPatternWheel.tsx`** / **`VerticalPatternDrum.tsx`** / **`VerticalWheel.tsx`**
+- **Role**: Custom gesture-driven pattern selectors. The arc wheel is the primary pattern picker in DockedController. The drum is the alternative vertical scroll variant.
+- **Why custom**: React Native's built-in `FlatList` picker has insufficient gesture control for a fast-swipe-to-pattern UX. These implement custom pan gesture handlers.
+
+**`CircularKnob.tsx`** / **`CustomSlider.tsx`**
+- **Role**: Reusable hardware-styled UI controls for brightness, speed, and EQ parameters.
+
+**`GroupSettingsModal.tsx`**
+- **Role**: Modal for creating or editing a device group (name + member device selection).
+- **Saves to**: `ng_custom_groups` AsyncStorage key via the `onSave` callback in DashboardScreen.
+
+**`DeviceItem.tsx`**
+- **Role**: Single device card in the BLE device roster list. Displays name, RSSI bars, connection status, and quick-connect button.
+
+**`CameraTracker.tsx`**
+- **Role**: Camera-based color extraction. Uses the device camera to sample ambient color and map it to live LED output.
+
+**`SpectrumVisualizer.tsx`**
+- **Role**: Microphone audio spectrum EQ visualizer bar display used in music mode.
+
+**`Header.tsx`**
+- **Role**: App top bar with logo and navigation controls. Minimal component.
+
+---
+
+### G. CONTEXT (`src/context/`)
+
+**`ThemeContext.tsx`**
+- **Role**: Global React context for light/dark/control theme selection. Persists preference to `@sk8lytz_theme` / `@sk8lytz_control_theme` AsyncStorage keys.
+- **Why**: Multiple components need theme state without prop drilling.
+
+---
+
+### H. CONSTANTS (`src/constants/`)
+
+**`RbmPatterns.ts`**
+- **Role**: Complete catalog of all 210 RBM (Running Business Mode) pattern definitions. Each entry includes a pattern ID (1-210), display name, category tag, and color preview.
+- **Why**: The pattern library is static hardware data that doesn't change. Centralizing it prevents inconsistencies between the pattern wheel UI and protocol payload generation.
+
+---
+
+### I. UTILS (`src/utils/`)
+
+**`RbmDictionary.ts`**
+- **Role**: Lookup helper that maps pattern IDs to names, and names back to IDs. Used by `DockedController` and `AppLogger` to resolve human-readable pattern names for the analytics event payload.
+
+**`MusicDictionary.ts`**
+- **Role**: Same pattern as `RbmDictionary` but for music sync mode IDs (modes 1-16). Maps mode ID ├óΓÇáΓÇÖ display name.
+

+### J. SUPABASE DATABASE SCHEMA
+
+**Project ID**: `qefmeivpjyaukbwadgaz`
+
+| Table | Purpose | Key Columns | RLS |
+|---|---|---|---|
+| `parsed_session_stats` | One row per app session summary | `session_id` (UNIQUE), `device_id`, `host_device_id`, `total_events`, `battery_level` | Append-only (public INSERT) |
+| `parsed_session_devices` | All BLE devices seen per session | `session_id + device_id` (UNIQUE), `name`, `rssi`, `firmware_ver`, `ic_type`, `led_points` | Append-only |
+| `parsed_logs` | Full event trace log | `session_id`, `device_id`, `device_name`, `event_type`, `group_id`, `group_name`, `raw_data` | Append-only |
+| `parsed_mode_usage` | Mode frequency per device | `session_id`, `device_id`, `device_name`, `mode_name`, `usage_count`, `group_id` | Append-only |
+| `parsed_pattern_usage` | Pattern frequency per device | `session_id`, `device_id`, `device_name`, `pattern_idx`, `usage_count`, `group_id` | Append-only |
+| `parsed_color_usage` | Color frequency per device | `session_id`, `device_id`, `device_name`, `hex_color`, `usage_count`, `group_id` | Append-only |
+| `shared_scenes` (NEW) | Cloud-synced user presets | `id`, `author_id` (auth.users), `scene_payload` (jsonb), `upvotes`, `downloads`, `is_public` | RLS: Viewable if `is_public`. Only author can `INSERT`/`UPDATE`/`DELETE`. |
+
+**Supporting Components**:
+- **`src/services/ScenesService.ts`**: Manages Supabase DB bindings for scenes, secure RPC upvote firing, and session retrieval.
+- **`src/components/CommunityModal.tsx`**: Renders `FlatList` UI displaying `ICloudScene` items mapped from Postgres.
+
+**RLS Policy Design**: All telemetry tables use `INSERT WITH CHECK (true)` for the public (anon) role. There is intentionally NO `SELECT` policy for anon ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ data can flow in from the app but cannot be read back without authenticated credentials. This prevents telemetry leakage via the public anon key.
+
+**Storage Bucket**: `sk8lytz-logs`
+- `logs_<bleMac>.json` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ merged session log files per primary device MAC
+- `sk8lytz-picks.json` ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ curated preset list (SK8Lytz Picks), fetched at app launch
+

+### L. BUG FIX LOG ├óΓé¼ΓÇ¥ April 5 2026 Session
+
+| Bug | Root Cause | Fix Applied |
+|---|---|---|
+| Custom device names never reached Supabase | AppLogger was reading `@device_settings_${MAC}` but DashboardScreen writes to `ng_device_configs` (different key, different format) | Fixed to read `ng_device_configs`, parse nested dict by MAC |
+| Duplicate rows in `parsed_session_devices` | `session_id` was `Date.now()` per upload call, creating a new session on every background push | Moved `sessionId` to singleton constructor; switched INSERT to UPSERT with `onConflict: 'session_id, device_id'` |
+| `device_id` null on non-device-specific events | Telemetry payload used `item.d?.deviceId \|\| null`, leaving global events (app open, scan) with no device | Changed to fallback to `primaryMacRaw` (the first connected device's MAC) |
+| Group events only logged once, not per device | Matrix aggregation and trace log push used single `targetDeviceId`, not the `deviceIds` array | Rewrote both to iterate `targets` array (forEach for maps, flatMap for trace) |
+| `parsed_logs` had `RAW_PAYLOAD` events | Filter was only applied to the local merged log, not enforced before DB push | Confirmed `currentRunLogs` filter `l.e !== 'RAW_PAYLOAD'` is applied before all DB operations |
